id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">EE Limited</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<table class="infobox Kingdom</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Key people</div></th><td class="agent" style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<a style="padding-right:0.5em;">Brands</th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<div class="plainlist nowrap">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Orange_UK" title="Orange UK">Orange</a> <small>(2010\xe2\x80\x932015)</small></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_UK" title="T-Mobile UK">T-Mobile</a> <small>(2010\xe2\x80\x932015)</small></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;">Owner</th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<a href="/wiki/BT_Group" title="BT Group">BT Group</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ee.co.uk">www<wbr />.ee<wbr />.co<wbr />.uk</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>EE</b> (formerly <b>Everything Everywhere</b>) is a British <a href="/wiki/Mobile_network_operator" title="Mobile network operator">mobile network operator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">internet service provider</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Division_(business)" title="Division (business)">division</a> of <a href="/wiki/BT_Group" title="BT Group">BT Group</a>. It was established in 2010 as a 50:50 joint venture between <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom</a> and France T\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9com (now <a href="/wiki/Orange_S.A." title="Orange S.A.">Orange S.A.</a>) through the merger of their respective <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_UK" title="T-Mobile UK">T-Mobile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orange_UK" title="Orange UK">Orange</a> businesses in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-merger_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-merger-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IndyMergerStory_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndyMergerStory-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It is the largest mobile network operator in the UK, with 29.6 million customers and the largest operator of <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a> services in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It was acquired by BT in January 2016 and subsequently became a second consumer division, operating alongside <a href="/wiki/BT_Consumer" title="BT Consumer">BT Consumer</a> following BT\'s new organisational structure that took effect in April 2016. It retained its brand, network and retail stores while its business operations became part of newly formed <a href="/wiki/BT_Business_and_Public_Sector" title="BT Business and Public Sector">BT Business and Public Sector</a> division, and its <a href="/wiki/Mobile_virtual_network_operator" title="Mobile virtual network operator">MVNO</a> operations became part of newly formed <a href="/wiki/BT_Wholesale_and_Ventures" title="BT Wholesale and Ventures">BT Wholesale and Ventures</a> division.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> On 28 July 2017, BT announced organisational changes to "simplify its operating model, strengthen accountabilities and accelerate its transformation" and involves bringing together its BT Consumer and EE divisions into a new unified BT Consumer division that will operate across three brands \xe2\x80\x93 BT, EE and <a href="/wiki/Plusnet" title="Plusnet">Plusnet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It will take effect from 1 April 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EE has its headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Hatfield,_Hertfordshire" title="Hatfield, Hertfordshire">Hatfield</a> in the UK and also has main offices in <a href="/wiki/BT_Centre" title="BT Centre">BT Centre</a> in London, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darlington" title="Darlington">Darlington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doxford_Park" title="Doxford Park">Doxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenock" title="Greenock">Greenock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merthyr_Tydfil" title="Merthyr Tydfil">Merthyr Tydfil</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Tyneside" title="North Tyneside">North Tyneside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>. As of 23 November 2016, EE\'s <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/2G" title="2G">2G</a> networks\' combined coverage reaches more than 99% of the UK population, with double speed 4G reaching 80% while EE\xe2\x80\x99s <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> network reaches 98% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Telegraph_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Telegraph-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg/280px-Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg" width="280" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg/420px-Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg/560px-Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="780" data-file-height="320" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hatfield_Business_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>EE\'s headquarters at Hatfield Business Park, previously the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_UK" title="T-Mobile UK">T-Mobile UK</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Deutsche Telekom and France T\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9com (now Orange S.A.) announced plans to merge their respective UK ventures <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_UK" title="T-Mobile UK">T-Mobile UK</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orange_UK" title="Orange UK">Orange UK</a> on 8 September 2009. The initial planning suggested a joint revenue of around \xc2\xa37.7 billion for 2008 with savings via synergies expected to total around "over \xc2\xa3445 million annually from 2014 onwards".<sup id="cite_ref-Plans_To_Form_Merger_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plans_To_Form_Merger-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The two companies also announced an expected investment of "\xc2\xa3600 to \xc2\xa3800 million in integration costs".<sup id="cite_ref-Plans_To_Form_Merger_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plans_To_Form_Merger-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The initial press release outlined a primarily clear vision for the two brands citing that "the T-Mobile UK and Orange UK brands will be maintained separately for 18 months".<sup id="cite_ref-Plans_To_Form_Merger_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plans_To_Form_Merger-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The merger was cleared by the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> on 1 March 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Everything_Everywhere_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Everything_Everywhere_logo.png/220px-Everything_Everywhere_logo.png" width="220" height="66" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Everything_Everywhere_logo.png/330px-Everything_Everywhere_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6e/Everything_Everywhere_logo.png 2x" data-file-width="438" data-file-height="131" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Everything_Everywhere_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Everything Everywhere logo used from 2010 until September 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>The joint venture was announced as completed on 1 April 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-Completion_of_Merger_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Completion_of_Merger-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and the name Everything Everywhere was announced on 11 May 2010. On the same day the company confirmed that "roaming across both networks [would be] due later in that year, at no additional cost to the customer" and further emphasised the separation of the brands at that present moment in time, saying that each brand would maintain "its own shops, marketing campaigns, propositions and service centres".<sup id="cite_ref-Unveiling_of_Name_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unveiling_of_Name-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The companies\' network sharing plans (allowing Orange customers to utilise T-Mobile\'s 2G signal and vice versa) were released to customers on 11 October 2010. The "switch-on" was rolled out utilising an opt-in page on each brand\'s website. However, the rollout did not initially include automatic network roaming mid-call or the two brands\' 3G services.<sup id="cite_ref-Big_Switch-On_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Big_Switch-On-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 July 2011, Tom Alexander announced unexpectedly that he would step down as CEO. Alexander had joined Orange in 2008 and had led the company since its formation on 1 July 2010. It was announced that he would leave his post on 31 August 2011 and therefore as from 1 September 2011, he would be replaced by Olaf Swantee, who had held the position of Executive VP of European Activities and Sourcing for France T\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9com in addition to being a member of EE\'s board.  Alexander said that he would remain with the company throughout the remainder of 2011 and continue to advise Swantee in his new role.<sup id="cite_ref-Olaf_Swantee_Appointed_CEO_of_Everything_Everywhere_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olaf_Swantee_Appointed_CEO_of_Everything_Everywhere-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  Swantee is seen as having done an exceptional job in leading the group through the challenges of rebranding and the launch of a new technology, and was named the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mobiletoday.co.uk/power50/2013/Olaf_Swantee/608">mobile industry\'s person of the year</a> in 2013 as a result. \n</p><p>On 2 November 2011 Everything Everywhere announced plans to cut a further 550 back office staff, with its sites in Bristol, Darlington, Hatfield, and Paddington affected.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2012, the T-Mobile network in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> was switched off, meaning that all customers there roam onto Orange. However, later<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2015)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> most T-Mobile sites were turned back on as EE has a mast sharing agreement with 3 (MBNL).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rebranding">Rebranding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rebranding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Everything Everywhere announced on 22 August 2012 that it would introduce a third brand as part of a future 4G launch to sit alongside Orange and T-Mobile, and that Everything Everywhere would continue as the company\'s legal name.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Further speculation commenced on 7 September 2012 when the company announced details of a press conference on the morning of 11 September 2012, the earliest date set by Ofcom to launch 4G services.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> It was also noted that this date was only 24 hours earlier than the expected launch of the latest generation of <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> (the iPhone 5), thereby arousing suspicion that the new iPhone would support 4G and that Everything Everywhere would launch its service on this widely anticipated handset.<sup id="cite_ref-Everything_Everywhere_Launching_New_Network_on_Tuesday_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Everything_Everywhere_Launching_New_Network_on_Tuesday-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Other commentators suggested that the <a href="/wiki/HTC_One_X" title="HTC One X">HTC One X</a>L would be the first handset to launch utilising Everything Everywhere\'s 4G network.<sup id="cite_ref-HTC_One_XL:_Everything_Everywhere&#39;s_first_4G_phone_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTC_One_XL:_Everything_Everywhere&#39;s_first_4G_phone-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The handsets that the company initially launched on EE are the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5" title="IPhone 5">iPhone 5</a> (<a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>), <a href="/wiki/HTC_One_X" title="HTC One X">HTC One X</a>L (<a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>), <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S_III" title="Samsung Galaxy S III">Samsung Galaxy S III</a> (Android), <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_Note_II" title="Samsung Galaxy Note II">Samsung Galaxy Note&#160;II</a> (Android), <a href="/wiki/Huawei_Ascend_P1" title="Huawei Ascend P1">Huawei Ascend P1</a> (Android), <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Lumia_920" title="Nokia Lumia 920">Nokia Lumia 920</a> (<a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">Windows Phone</a>), <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Lumia_820" title="Nokia Lumia 820">Nokia Lumia 820</a> (Windows Phone). The company also announced that they would be using two 4G mobile broadband devices manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a> - the <a href="/wiki/Huawei_E5#E589" title="Huawei E5">E589 Mobile Wi-Fi device</a> and E392 mobile broadband dongle.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company announced on 11 September 2012 that the EE brand would be used to identify its network on all of the company\'s devices (EE, Orange and T-Mobile), alongside its 4G service and the company\'s fibre optic broadband roll-out. The brand was described by EE as <i>The Super Fast Brand</i>. It was also confirmed that all ex-Orange and ex-T-Mobile shops would be re-branded EE overnight, but that mobile products would continue to be sold under those brands inside the stores.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The company\'s legal name changed to EE Limited on 2 September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EE announced on 30 October 2012 that its Orange broadband service would be rebranded as EE, and the company would be launching a new <a href="/wiki/Fiber-optic_communication" title="Fiber-optic communication">fibre-optic</a> broadband service, using a Bright Box router and  Openreach GEA.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The change took effect on 5 November 2012 through a firmware upgrade that replaced the Orange branding with EE on customers\' router web interface.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2014, EE began to phase out the Orange and T-Mobile brands in the UK, removing these products from their website and retail stores. However, Orange/T-Mobile plans were still available via telesales and through third-party retail channels. The phase out was completed in March 2015, with new connections and upgrades only available on EE branded services.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Existing customers will remain on their Orange or T-Mobile contracts until they upgrade.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_years_and_acquisition_by_BT">Recent years and acquisition by BT</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Recent years and acquisition by BT">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 5 November 2013, EE began testing <a href="/wiki/LTE_Advanced" title="LTE Advanced">LTE Advanced</a> (LTE-A) in <a href="/wiki/East_London_Tech_City" title="East London Tech City">East London Tech City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The LTE-A network offered speeds up to 300 Mbit/s when rolled out to the public in 2014. EE\'s LTE-Advanced was launched at the end of October 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During 2014, <a href="/wiki/Orange_S.A." title="Orange S.A.">Orange S.A.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom</a> were reported to be considering options to sell EE or divest it through an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On 15 December 2014, <a href="/wiki/BT_Group" title="BT Group">BT Group</a> confirmed that it had entered into exclusive talks to buy EE for \xc2\xa312.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On 5 February 2015, BT confirmed it would be acquiring EE for \xc2\xa312.5 billion; subject to regulatory approval,<sup id="cite_ref-BT_acquisition_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT_acquisition-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and received final unconditional approval by the <a href="/wiki/Competition_and_Markets_Authority" title="Competition and Markets Authority">Competition and Markets Authority</a> on 15 January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-CMA_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMA-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The deal was officially completed on 29 January 2016 with Deutsche Telekom now owning 12% of BT, while Orange owns 4%.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 February 2016, <a href="/wiki/BT_Group" title="BT Group">BT Group</a> announced that EE will become a new consumer division within the wider group, alongside <a href="/wiki/BT_Consumer" title="BT Consumer">BT Consumer</a>. It will serve customers with mobile services, broadband and TV, and also continue to deliver the Emergency Services Network contract which was awarded to EE in late 2015. EE\'s existing business division will be brought together with <a href="/wiki/BT_Business" class="mw-redirect" title="BT Business">BT Business</a> and the UK-focused operations of <a href="/wiki/BT_Global_Services" title="BT Global Services">BT Global Services</a> to form a new BT Business and Public Sector division with around \xc2\xa35bn of revenues. There will also be another new division; BT Wholesale and Ventures that will comprise the existing <a href="/wiki/BT_Wholesale" class="mw-redirect" title="BT Wholesale">BT Wholesale</a> division along with EE\'s <a href="/wiki/Mobile_virtual_network_operator" title="Mobile virtual network operator">MVNO</a> business as well as some specialist businesses such as Fleet, Payphones and Directories. Gerry McQuade, currently Chief Sales and Marketing Officer, Business at EE, will be its CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>EE has main offices in <a href="/wiki/BT_Centre" title="BT Centre">BT Centre</a> in London, <a href="/wiki/Hatfield,_Hertfordshire" title="Hatfield, Hertfordshire">Hatfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darlington" title="Darlington">Darlington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doxford_Park" title="Doxford Park">Doxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenock" title="Greenock">Greenock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merthyr_Tydfil" title="Merthyr Tydfil">Merthyr Tydfil</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Tyneside" title="North Tyneside">North Tyneside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>. EE owns and operates national <a href="/wiki/2G" title="2G">2G</a>, <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> and <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a> mobile phone networks in the UK. It also has around 700 retail outlets across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 June 2016, it was announced that EE was making preparations to move from its London-based offices in <a href="/wiki/Paddington" title="Paddington">Paddington</a> to BT Centre at the end of year, as part of BT\'s plans to save \xc2\xa3360 million a year following its acquisition of EE.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The move was initiated on 28 November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="4G_network">4G network</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 4G network">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Everything Everywhere\'s request to use its surplus capacity to launch 4G services in the UK was approved by <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a> on 21 August 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Everything_Everywhere_gets_up_to_a_year&#39;s_head_start_in_4G_race_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Everything_Everywhere_gets_up_to_a_year&#39;s_head_start_in_4G_race-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> As part of Ofcom\'s approval of the company\'s roll-out of 4G it was announced on 22 August 2012 that <a href="/wiki/Hutchison_3G" class="mw-redirect" title="Hutchison 3G">Hutchison 3G</a> had acquired part of Everything Everywhere\'s 1800&#160;MHz spectrum.<sup id="cite_ref-Everything_Everywhere_sells_services_to_3_allowing_for_4G_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Everything_Everywhere_sells_services_to_3_allowing_for_4G-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EE\'s 4G network along with its nationwide marketing campaign and store re-branding was officially launched on 30 October 2012. 4G coverage was initially "switched on" in 11 UK cities; London, Bristol, Birmingham, Cardiff, Edinburgh, Glasgow, Leeds, Liverpool, Manchester, Sheffield, and Southampton.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\nDuring the latter part of 2012 and 2013, the company added more cities and towns,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and planned to boost speeds in some existing locations by Summer 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> EE claims 2,000 square miles of 4G network would be added every month from launch and the goal is to cover 70 per cent of the population by the end of 2013, and 90 per cent by the end of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EE had early problems and issues of no signal across both its 3G and 4G networks with senior EE staff conceding they were facing \'teething problems\'.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 February 2013, Ofcom announced that EE had been awarded more 4G spectrum in the 800&#160;MHz and 2.6&#160;GHz bands, bidding around \xc2\xa3588&#160;million for the spectrum.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 12 February 2016, EE announced that it had reached its 2015 targets to double the number of 4G users on its network to 14 million at the year\xe2\x80\x99s end and remains as Europe\xe2\x80\x99s largest 4G operator. Its <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a> network now reaches more than 95% of the UK population, with double speed 4G reaching 80%. EE\xe2\x80\x99s <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> network reaches 98% of the population while its <a href="/wiki/2G" title="2G">2G</a> network reaches 99%.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Telegraph_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Telegraph-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 April 2016, it was announced that as part of a new strategy, EE are aiming to extend the geographic reach of its 4G network in the UK from the current 60% to 95% by 2020, which will increase the proportion of the UK\xe2\x80\x99s population covered by the 4G network from 95% to 99.8%. In order to achieve this, EE will build more than 750 new sites. Its 4G network was switched on today in <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>, enabled by the fibre broadband links deployed by BT. Its 4G network at launch was only used for data connections, with customers moving to 3G while on a call, however EE are now rolling out 4G Calling (<a href="/wiki/Voice_over_LTE" title="Voice over LTE">VoLTE</a>) across the UK to allow both voice and data over 4G as well as allowing customers to make calls in new areas of the network that are 4G-only. 4G Calling is already live in London, Birmingham, Bristol, Manchester, Edinburgh, Glasgow, Belfast, Leeds and Newcastle, and will be switched on across the rest of the network by July.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 September 2017, it was announced that EE are upgrading its 4G network by converting airwaves from 2G to 4G. It currently uses frequencies in the 1800&#160;MHz band for both 2G and 4G (its other bands are reserved solely for 3G/4G) and is converting \xe2\x80\x93 or \xe2\x80\x98refarming\xe2\x80\x99 10&#160;MHz of the 2G airwaves and adding that to the existing 20&#160;MHz slice that\'s already configured for 4G. More than 600 sites across cities including London, Birmingham, Manchester, Edinburgh and Cardiff, will be upgraded with the latest 4G spectrum over the next six months, equipped with \xe2\x80\x98Cat 12\xe2\x80\x99 and \xe2\x80\x98Cat 16\xe2\x80\x99 modems which will provide better speeds and coverage and support next generation \xe2\x80\x98CAT 12\xe2\x80\x99 and \'CAT 16\' smartphones. The data upload speeds will also be doubled from the current maximum of 50Mbps to up to 100Mbps on more than 900 sites across the UK. It is also expanding its UK-wide 4G+ with more than 1,000 sites supporting \xe2\x80\x98Cat 9\xe2\x80\x99 speeds above 400Mbps. The geographic reach of its 4G network is now 85%.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 March 2018, it was announced that EE had filled 12,000 <a href="/wiki/Square_kilometre" title="Square kilometre">square kilometres</a> of mobile not-spots in the last 12 months; equivalent of more than 1.5 million <a href="/wiki/Football_pitch" title="Football pitch">football pitches</a> as part of its 4G geographic reach strategy of 95% by 2020, currently 90%. This involved upgrading more than 4,000 existing <a href="/wiki/Cell_site" title="Cell site">sites</a> to provide 4G, and the construction of 105 new sites which are spread across <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Wales" title="North Wales">North Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and is in the process of building a further 350 new sites to continue filling in mobile not-spots. Many of these new sites are in areas that have previously had no coverage from any operator and have already carried more than 200 <a href="/wiki/999_(emergency_telephone_number)#United_Kingdom" title="999 (emergency telephone number)">emergency 999 calls</a> where people would have previously been unable to call for help. The new sites are being built to provide coverage for EE\xe2\x80\x99s customers and for the Emergency Services Network. The geographic reach of its 4G network in Scotland surpassed 75% at the end of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 September 2018, it was announced that EE are upgrading its 4G network by converting airwaves from 3G to 4G. It currently uses frequencies in the 2100&#160;MHz band for 3G and is converting \xe2\x80\x93 or \xe2\x80\x98refarming\xe2\x80\x99 it for 4G. More than 500 <a href="/wiki/Cell_site" title="Cell site">sites</a> will be upgraded in the next six months and are the busiest \xe2\x80\x98hotspots\xe2\x80\x99 in its network where there is the greatest demand for <a href="/wiki/Internet_access#Mobile_broadband" title="Internet access">mobile data</a>. These sites are spread across cities including London, Birmingham, Manchester, Bristol, Exeter, Hull, Nottingham, Edinburgh, Glasgow, Cardiff and Belfast. In addition to providing better speeds and reliability, these sites will provide five \xe2\x80\x98carriers\xe2\x80\x99 of 4G which is more than any other UK operator and accommodate the latest smartphones which can support connections to all five at the same time, with Five Carrier Aggregation (5CA). It also lays the foundation for its <a href="/wiki/5G" title="5G">5G</a> network that will be launched in 2019 where it will be built on top of the upgraded sites. The geographic reach of its 4G network is now 91%.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_payments">Mobile payments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mobile payments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 27 January 2011, Everything Everywhere and <a href="/wiki/Barclaycard" title="Barclaycard">Barclaycard</a> announced that they would be jointly introducing the UK\'s first contactless mobile payments system for consumers by early summer 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Everything Everywhere expanded its contactless mobile payments arm by announcing a deal with <a href="/wiki/Mastercard" title="Mastercard">Mastercard</a> on 28 August 2012 that would see the two companies work together on introducing <a href="/wiki/Near_field_communication" class="mw-redirect" title="Near field communication">Near field communication</a> (NFC) technology and other mobile payment technologies into the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Everything Everywhere sustained its involvement in the future of NFC technology in the UK by announcing a joint venture between itself, <a href="/wiki/Vodafone" title="Vodafone">Vodafone</a> and <a href="/wiki/O2_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="O2 (United Kingdom)">O2</a>. The joint venture was designed to be a "single point of contact" for all those involved in increasing the adoption of using NFC for mobile payments in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Regulators_approve_UK_mobile_payment_joint_venture_between_Everything_Everywhere,_Vodafone_and_O2_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regulators_approve_UK_mobile_payment_joint_venture_between_Everything_Everywhere,_Vodafone_and_O2-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 November 2012 it was announced that EE had exclusively partnered with mobile payments company <a href="/wiki/IZettle" title="IZettle">iZettle</a>. The agreement allowed EE to sell the company\'s mini debit/credit card readers which allow small business customers to make payments using their mobile phones. The devices initially went on sale in 297 EE stores and via EE\xe2\x80\x99s telesales channel.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HD_voice_calling">HD voice calling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: HD voice calling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 22 June 2010, Everything Everywhere announced plans to roll out <a href="/wiki/Wideband_audio" title="Wideband audio">HD voice calling</a> throughout its network by the end of summer. The technology was initially trialled on Orange\'s network in <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Berkshire" title="Reading, Berkshire">Reading</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a>, before it was expanded to the rest of the UK by the end of summer.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Smart_number_technology">Smart number technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Smart number technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 11 June 2018, EE became the first UK network to launch smart number technology, allowing customers to use the same number across multiple devices in addition to their <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a> including <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smartwatch" title="Smartwatch">smartwatches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laptop" title="Laptop">laptops</a>. It is available at no extra cost to new and existing customers and is part of its strategy to "keep customers connected by bringing together the best of mobile and broadband through first-of-their-kind converged services across the UK". It supports calls and texts across multiple devices and works even when they don\xe2\x80\x99t have their smartphone with them. It supports up to 5 other connected devices and will need to be internet connected via Wi-Fi or mobile, with the primary device being connected to the EE network for the service to work. Calls can be made on multiple devices at the same time, or handed off between devices.\n</p><p>It is available initially on <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> devices, with <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> devices coming at a later date. Customers will need to be on a EE pay monthly plan on their smartphone with minimum <a href="/wiki/IOS_11#11.3" title="IOS 11">iOS 11.3</a> on <a href="/wiki/IPhone_6" title="IPhone 6">iPhone 6</a> or later. Paired <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPads</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macintosh" title="Macintosh">Macs</a> will need to be on minimum <a href="/wiki/IOS_10" title="IOS 10">iOS 10</a> and <a href="/wiki/OS_X_El_Capitan" title="OS X El Capitan">OS X El Capitan</a> respectively, <a href="/wiki/IPod_Touch" title="IPod Touch">iPod Touch</a> with minimum iOS 10 and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Watch" title="Apple Watch">Apple Watch</a> with minimum <a href="/wiki/WatchOS" title="WatchOS">watchOS 2</a>. EE is also the only UK network to support the full connected capability of the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Watch_Series_3" title="Apple Watch Series 3">Apple Watch Series 3</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadband">Broadband</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Broadband">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>EE inherited the <a href="/wiki/Orange_UK#Services" title="Orange UK">Orange UK broadband service</a>, and as of April 2015 EE had around 900,000 broadband customers.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> EE also offer a TV service which uses Freeview.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retail_stores">Retail stores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Retail stores">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EE,_Kirkgate,_Bradford_(8th_November_2014).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/EE%2C_Kirkgate%2C_Bradford_%288th_November_2014%29.JPG/220px-EE%2C_Kirkgate%2C_Bradford_%288th_November_2014%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/EE%2C_Kirkgate%2C_Bradford_%288th_November_2014%29.JPG/330px-EE%2C_Kirkgate%2C_Bradford_%288th_November_2014%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/EE%2C_Kirkgate%2C_Bradford_%288th_November_2014%29.JPG/440px-EE%2C_Kirkgate%2C_Bradford_%288th_November_2014%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EE,_Kirkgate,_Bradford_(8th_November_2014).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An EE store in Kirkgate, Bradford, 2014</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EE_mobile_phones,_Oxford_Street,_London,_March_2016_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/EE_mobile_phones%2C_Oxford_Street%2C_London%2C_March_2016_01.jpg/220px-EE_mobile_phones%2C_Oxford_Street%2C_London%2C_March_2016_01.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/EE_mobile_phones%2C_Oxford_Street%2C_London%2C_March_2016_01.jpg/330px-EE_mobile_phones%2C_Oxford_Street%2C_London%2C_March_2016_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/EE_mobile_phones%2C_Oxford_Street%2C_London%2C_March_2016_01.jpg/440px-EE_mobile_phones%2C_Oxford_Street%2C_London%2C_March_2016_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EE_mobile_phones,_Oxford_Street,_London,_March_2016_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An EE store in <a href="/wiki/Oxford_Street" title="Oxford Street">Oxford Street</a>, London, 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>In November 2010, EE announced further connections between the two brands by announcing the opening of six "dual-branded stores" in <a href="/wiki/Tooting" title="Tooting">Tooting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palmers_Green" title="Palmers Green">Palmers Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hertford" title="Hertford">Hertford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridgend" title="Bridgend">Bridgend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weston-super-Mare" title="Weston-super-Mare">Weston-super-Mare</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Dorset" title="Dorchester, Dorset">Dorchester</a>. The six new stores were described as "concession-within-stores". This meant that a selection of Orange propositions would be sold and promoted in the three T-Mobile stores being opened and that a range of T-Mobile propositions would be merchandised in the three Orange stores. They were described as concessions as the host brand would take the overall lead.<sup id="cite_ref-Concession_Stores_Announced_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concession_Stores_Announced-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company further expanded in retail over the following months by announcing five "new trial stores". These stores sell both brands\' products, services and accessories; they were also designed to a give an "inspire, excite and educate" experience.<sup id="cite_ref-New_Look_Stores_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Look_Stores-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>  Each store has an externally Everything Everywhere\xe2\x80\x93branded fascia, however it also maintains a continued emphasis that the stores represent and sell both Orange and T-Mobile. The first store launch was in <a href="/wiki/Altrincham" title="Altrincham">Altrincham</a> on 18 February 2010, a little over a week after the initial announcement on 10 February 2010. The other stores were launched in <a href="/wiki/Bishop%27s_Stortford" title="Bishop&#39;s Stortford">Bishop\'s Stortford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eltham" title="Eltham">Eltham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lowestoft" title="Lowestoft">Lowestoft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evesham" title="Evesham">Evesham</a> within four weeks of the <a href="/wiki/Altrincham" title="Altrincham">Altrincham</a> shop launch. Everything Everywhere made a concerted effort to launch stores in "white-spot areas", or stores where they had little or no existing footprint from Orange or T-Mobile.<sup id="cite_ref-New_Look_Stores_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Look_Stores-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>  During the same quarter, the company also launched a number of Orange concessions in selected <a href="/wiki/HMV" title="HMV">HMV</a> stores. These were designed to operate as normal Orange retail stores, however with an expected lower footfall and designed to cater for HMV\'s younger consumers.<sup id="cite_ref-New_Look_Stores_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Look_Stores-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The company removed all of these concessions from HMV shortly before the re-brand with the approximately 100 staff employed within them transferred to local stores.<sup id="cite_ref-Orange_removes_its_concessions_from_HMV_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Orange_removes_its_concessions_from_HMV-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EE now operates 700 retail stores in the UK after the re-branding of existing Orange, T-Mobile, and Everything Everywhere stores in October 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> On 17 January 2013, it was announced that EE would close 78 stores in February 2013 with no job losses because in several locations it then had two stores on the same street, often close together.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On 10 January 2014, it was announced that EE would close a further 76 duplicated stores and announced plans to open 50 new stores, including 30 franchise outlets that will all be EE branded in 2014 as part of its wider retail improvement programme, and is estimated to create 350 new jobs. Its total number of franchise outlets will grow from the current 25 to 100 by the end of the year which includes the transfer of 45 directly managed stores to franchise partners. The move sees its total number of retail stores reduce from 600 to 574 (including 100 franchise outlets).<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 22 September 2014, it was announced that following the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Phones_4u" title="Phones 4u">Phones 4u</a> in the UK, EE will acquire 58 of its stores for \xc2\xa32.5 million in a deal with its administrators, <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a>. The deal safeguards 359 jobs and the stores will be rebranded to EE, with plans to open most by next week.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 July 2017, it was announced that EE are expanding its retail presence with a further 100 stores as a <a href="/wiki/Store-within-a-store" title="Store-within-a-store">store-within-a-store</a> by the end of 2019 via a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s" title="Sainsbury&#39;s">Sainsbury\'s</a>. It will create 400 new jobs in Sainsbury\xe2\x80\x99s and <a href="/wiki/Argos_(retailer)" title="Argos (retailer)">Argos</a> stores and sees its total number of retail stores reach close to 700, as part of its ambition to provide 95% of the population with access to an EE store within 20 minutes\xe2\x80\x99 drive. It is also launching a variety of new store formats: "EE \xe2\x80\x98Showcase\xe2\x80\x99 stores will contain dedicated Help Hubs for customer service and areas to experience new technologies; pop-up shops and cabins will appear in shopping centres and other locations around the UK; and mobile EE shops in vans will serve customers in the most remote areas".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Virtual_network_agreements">Virtual network agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Virtual network agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Mobile_UK" title="Virgin Mobile UK">Virgin Mobile UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Co-operative_Mobile" class="mw-redirect" title="The Co-operative Mobile">The Co-operative Mobile</a> <sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/ASDA_Mobile" class="mw-redirect" title="ASDA Mobile">Asda Mobile</a> operate on the EE network under a <a href="/wiki/Mobile_virtual_network_operator" title="Mobile virtual network operator">MVNO agreement</a>, which was most recently renegotiated in December 2010 for Virgin, and November 2013 for Asda (which had previously operated on the <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_UK" title="Vodafone UK">Vodafone</a> network).<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/BT_Mobile" title="BT Mobile">BT Mobile</a> and EE also have an MVNO agreement, which has allowed <a href="/wiki/BT_Mobile" title="BT Mobile">BT Mobile</a> to offer packages since March 2014.\n</p><p>EE purchased LIFE Mobile in October 2014, a MVNO set up by <a href="/wiki/Phones_4u" title="Phones 4u">Phones 4u</a> in 2013 from <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PWC</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Joint_venture_with_Hutchison_3G_UK">Joint venture with Hutchison 3G UK</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Joint venture with Hutchison 3G UK">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 3 September 2010, Everything Everywhere announced that Orange would join <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Broadband_Network_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile Broadband Network Limited">Mobile Broadband Network Limited</a> (MBNL), the <a href="/wiki/3G_network" class="mw-redirect" title="3G network">3G network</a> sharing joint venture formed in December 2007 between T-Mobile UK and Hutchison 3G UK (H3G UK). MBNL would become a 50/50 joint venture between Three UK and Everything Everywhere, with Orange contributing several thousand of its base stations for network sharing purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-telegeography.com_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegeography.com-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> MBNL was created after T-Mobile and Three UK agreed to pool their respective 3G infrastructures in a 50/50 joint venture. By September 2010 MBNL\xe2\x80\x99s HSPA-based infrastructure covered more than 90% of the British population, and was expected to rise to more than 98% by the end of 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-telegeography.com_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegeography.com-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_frequency_summary">Radio frequency summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Radio class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>EE launched its first television advertisement on 3 November 2012, four days after the company launched its 4G services and new brand. The advertisements featured <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Bacon" title="Kevin Bacon">Kevin Bacon</a> and his related <a href="/wiki/Six_Degrees_of_Kevin_Bacon" title="Six Degrees of Kevin Bacon">Six Degrees of Kevin Bacon</a> concept. The advert initially aired on <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> during <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor</a></i>, on its Saturday evening slot on UK television.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The adverts were filmed over two days during August 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Lewes" title="Lewes">Lewes</a>. EE also did a new online <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.smokingrocket.co.uk/smoking-rocket-in-the-new-ee-wifi-calling-advert/">advert</a> for WIFI calling in 2015 featuring <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.smokingrocket.co.uk/">Smoking Rocket</a> based in Aylesbury, you can read the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ee.co.uk/business/large/why-ee/4gee-case-studies/smoking-rocket">case study</a> on the EE Website.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships">Sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sponsorships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>EE began sponsoring the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">British Academy of Film and Television Arts</a> awards in 2013, replacing its Orange brand.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A six-year agreement to sponsor <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> was agreed with <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The Football Association</a> in February 2014, although was not classed as a naming rights agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EE had a presence at the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival_of_Contemporary_Performing_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Glastonbury Festival of Contemporary Performing Arts">Glastonbury Festival</a> 2015, providing reusable chargers for mobile phone users. The "Power Bars" could be exchanged once a day, for a fully charged charger, at two locations around the festival.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EE_Charging_Station_-_Glastonbury_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/EE_Charging_Station_-_Glastonbury_2015.jpg/220px-EE_Charging_Station_-_Glastonbury_2015.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/EE_Charging_Station_-_Glastonbury_2015.jpg/330px-EE_Charging_Station_-_Glastonbury_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/EE_Charging_Station_-_Glastonbury_2015.jpg/440px-EE_Charging_Station_-_Glastonbury_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EE_Charging_Station_-_Glastonbury_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>EE Power Bar at Glastonbury Festival of Contemporary Performing Arts 2015</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_and_controversies">Criticism and controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Criticism and controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In early 2013, <a href="/wiki/Ipsos_MORI" title="Ipsos MORI">Ipsos MORI</a> signed an agreement with EE, wherein Ipsos MORI would commercialise the data on the company\'s 23 million subscribers, for example "how many of the phone users checked their Facebook accounts, or the website of their favourite shop".<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> revealed that Ipsos MORI had negotiated an agreement to sell this data to the police and other parties. The data included "gender, age, postcode, websites visited, time of day text is sent [and] location of customer when call is made". When confronted by the paper, the police indicated that they would no longer go ahead with the deal. Ipsos MORI defended its actions, while EE refused to comment.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2013, T-Mobile UK was embroiled in a mid-contract increase controversy when it applied an above Retail Price Index increase to many contract customers but refused to allow termination as allowed by the terms of the contract. A number of customers complained to <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cisas.org.uk/">CISAS</a> about the conduct of T-Mobile UK, and its handling of the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2014, EE started a new service where customers could queue-jump when phoning EE customer services for a one off cost of 50p to be fast tracked out of the queue to an available agent. This sparked outrage among consumers who viewed the option as at extortionate charge for being put through promptly to a member of staff; something which should be standard.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Later that month, EE was accused of trying to silence complaining customers on social media networks, such as <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>. Customers claimed that the company deleted their complaints on the company\'s Facebook page. The company discourages customers from posting their grievances in public, preferring private messages.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2015, EE became the most complained-about phone and broadband provider, according to regulator, <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a>. Complaints against the UK\'s largest mobile operator related to topics ranging from line faults, service and provision issues to bill problems.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2017, EE were fined \xc2\xa32.7 million by the regulator, Ofcom, for overcharging more than 32,145 customers. Despite calls to the EE telephone number from within the EU becoming free from 18 November 2015, EE continued to bill more than 7,600 customers until January 2016. The fine was also applied as punishment for users calling the 150 customer services number whilst roaming within the EU being charged as though they were calling from the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2017, <a href="/wiki/Citizen%27s_Advice_Bureau" class="mw-redirect" title="Citizen&#39;s Advice Bureau">Citizen\'s Advice Bureau</a> undertook a mystery shopping exercise which found that EE along with <a href="/wiki/Vodafone" title="Vodafone">Vodafone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Three_UK" title="Three UK">Three</a> were not reducing customers\' bills after fixed deals finished meaning that they were paying an extra \xc2\xa322 a month on average. More for certain phones.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2018, a <a href="/wiki/White_hat_(computer_security)" title="White hat (computer security)">security researcher</a> discovered the company had failed to update the default administer\'s password on a <a href="/wiki/SonarQube" title="SonarQube">code quality testing platform</a> containing application source code and Amazon Web Services and API keys.  The company issued a statement saying "No customer data is, or has been, at risk." while the researcher pointed to the possibility of "Malicious hackers could analyze the code of their payment systems, and find major holes that could lead to theft of payment information"<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Later that month, EE blocked and removed a website after <a href="/wiki/Text_messaging" title="Text messaging">text messages</a> claiming to be from EE were sent to customers offering 40 percent off their monthly bills in celebration of the <a href="/wiki/Wedding_of_Prince_Harry_and_Meghan_Markle" title="Wedding of Prince Harry and Meghan Markle">Royal Wedding</a>. Customers took to <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a> to complain of the texts. The <a href="/wiki/Phishing" title="Phishing">scam messages</a> contained a link to a fake EE website, encouraging them to enter their <a href="/wiki/Personally_identifiable_information" title="Personally identifiable information">personal details</a> and <a href="/wiki/Payment_card_number" title="Payment card number">card number</a>. EE advised any customers who receive any messages to not click on any of the links, and delete the messages after forwarding them to 7726, <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a>\xe2\x80\x99s anti-spam service.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=EE_Limited&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ee.co.uk/our-company/about-ee/leadership-team">"Our team"</a>.
